Jamison Brereton

108 (934)
Sarama╠Д and the Pan╠гis
Saram─Б and Paс╣Зis
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
In the interpretation of this well-known and delightful dialogue hymn we follow the compelling study by Hanns-Peter Schmidt in his Br╠еhaspati und Indra (1968: 185тАУ 89). This dialogue takes place in the midst of a narrative whose outlines are clear, even if its details are not. The Paс╣Зis have entrapped cattle in a cave. Indra and the ancient Vedic seers wish to release the cattle. Therefore, Indra sends his dog Saram─Б to track down the Paс╣Зis and to demand the release of the cattle. She crosses the Ras─Б, the river at the border of the world that separates heaven and earth, and finds the Paс╣Зis. The Paс╣Зis refuse to surrender the cattle, however, and at the end Indra and the seersтАФthe Aс╣Еgirases and NavagvasтАФthemselves come to the place where the Paс╣Зis have hidden the cattle. They break open the cave through the power of the hymns they compose and chant. Because IndraтАЩs weapon in this story is not the vajra, the mace with which he destroys Vr╠еtra, but the truth embodied in the hymns that Indra and the seers recite, Indra is here called Br╠еhaspati, тАЬLord of the Sacred Formulation.тАЭ
The story also tells of the coming of the dawns, since the power of IndraтАЩs and the seerтАЩs words lies in the secret truth that the cattle are the dawns. Note that at the end, the poet uses the power of this truth for his own ends: through the truth of his hymn, he should acquire or recover cattle.
Despite the seriousness of the theme, it is hard to believe that the audience did not relish the depiction of a talking dog, especially one as saucy and forthright as the faithful Saram─Б, who resists the offered blandishments of the Paс╣Зis, to remain loyal to her master Indra.

тАЬ(The Paс╣Зis). With what intention has Saram─Б come to this plural ce? Verily the way is long and difficultto be traversed by the person vering. What is the motive of your coming to us? What sort of wandering was yours?How have you crossed the waters of the Ras─Б?тАЭ

Legend: The cows of Bс╣Ыhaspati had been stolen by the Paс╣Зis,the followers of the Asura Vala. At Bс╣Ыhaspati’s instrumental nce, Indra sent Saram─Б in search of the cattle. She havingcrossed a large river arrived at Vala’s stronghold and discovered the cattle. The Paс╣Зis trying to make friendswith her, the dialogue contained in this s┼лkta then ensued. ras─Б: the river of the firmament

Jamison Brereton

[Paс╣Зi:] Seeking what has Saram─Б arrived here, for far is the road,
swallowing up (the traveler) in the distance?
What is your mission to us? What was the final turn (bringing you here)? How did you cross the waters of the Ras─Б?

Griffith

WHAT wish of Sarama hath brought her hither? The path leads far away to distant places.
What charge hast thou for us? Where turns thy journey? How hast thou made thy way o’er Rasa’s waters.

Macdonell

With what desire has Saram─Б come hither? For weary is the way and far the distance. What was for us the message, what her roaming? How didst thou pass across the Ras─Б’s waters?

This hath preserved me from the fear of crossing: thus have I made my way o’er Rasa’s waters.

Jamison Brereton

[Paс╣Зi:] Of what sort is Indra, Saram─Б? What is his appearance?тАФhe as whose messenger you raced here from afar?
If he will come here, we will make an alliance with him, and then he will become the cowherd of our cattle.

Griffith

What is that Indra like, what is his aspect whose envoy, Sarama, from afar thou comest?
Let him approach, and we will show him friendship: he shall be made the herdsman of our cattle.

Macdonell

What, Saram─Б, is Indra like, as envoy For whom thou comest from the farthest distance? Let him come here: we will make him our comrade. So let him be the herdsman of our cattle.

Geldner

Grassmann

Jamison Brereton

[Saram─Б:] I know him not as one who can be deceived. He will deceive!тАФ he as whose messenger I raced here from afar.
Deep flowing rivers do not hide him. Smashed by Indra, Paс╣Зis, you will lie still.

Griffith

I know him safe from harm: but he can punish who sent me hither from afar as envoy.
Him rivers flowing with deep waters bide not. Low will ye be, O Panis, slain by Indra.

Macdonell

I know he can’t be harmed, but injures others, He as whose envoy from afar I come here. Deep-flowing streams cannot conceal his body: By Indra slain, ye shall lie prostrate, Paс╣Зis.

Jamison Brereton

[Paс╣Зi:] These cattle that you sought, Saram─Б, as you were flying around the ends of heaven, fortunate oneтАФ
who will release them to you without a fight? And our battle weapons are sharp!

Griffith

These are the kine which, Sarama, thou seekest, flying, O Blest One, to the ends of heaven.
Who will loose these for thee without a battle? Yea, and sharp-pointed are our warlike weapons.

Macdonell

Those cows for which, O Saram─Б, thou soughtest, Around the ends of heaven flying, fair one: Who them to thee would leave without resistance? And sharp indeed our weapons are in conflict.

Geldner

Jamison Brereton

[Saram─Б:] Your words are no weapons, Paс╣Зis! Let your evil bodies be impervious to arrows
or let the path to you be impossible to followтАФeither way, Br╠еhaspati will have no mercy on you!

Griffith

Even if your wicked bodies, O ye Panis, were arrow-proof, your words are weak for wounding;
And were the path to you as yet unmastered, Brhaspati in neither case will spare you.

Macdonell

Though these your words can not be fought with missiles, Nor those mis-shapen bodies pierced by arrows, Nor yet the road be forced, to reach your stronghold: Bс╣Ыhaspati will never spare you, Paс╣Зis.

Geldner

Eure Worte, Pani┬┤s, machen keine Soldaten. M├╢gen eure schlechten Leiber gegen Pfeile gefeit sein, mag der Weg, um zu euch zu gelangen, unerzwinglich sein: in beiden F├дllen wird Brihaspati euer nicht schonen.

Grassmann

┬╗Nicht treffend sind, o Pani’s, eure Worte; und w├дren schussfest eure b├╢sen Leiber, Und undurchdringlich auch der Weg zu euch hin, Brihaspati wird beides nicht verschonen.┬л

Jamison Brereton

[Paс╣Зi:] This treasury with its foundation of rock is overflowing with cows, horses, and goods, Saram─Б.
The Paс╣Зis, who are good herdsmen, guard it. In vain have you come on an empty track.

Griffith

Paved with the rock is this our treasure-chamber; filled full of precious things, of kine, and horses.
These Panis who are watchful keepers guard it. In vain hast thou approached this lonely station.

Macdonell

This treasure, Saram─Б, on rock is founded. Replete with goods, and cows, and horses. The Paс╣Зis here, its stout protectors, guard it: In vain thou comest to a fort unyielding.

Geldner

Diese Schatzkammer auf felsigem Grund ist voll von Rindern, Rossen, Sch├дtzen, o Sarama. Die Pani┬┤s, die gute W├дchter sind, beh├╝ten die. Du bist vergebens die falsche F├дhrte gegangen.

Grassmann

┬╗Auf Felsgrund ruht, o Saram─Б, der Schatz hier; gef├╝llt mit Rindern, Rossen und mit G├╝tern, Als gute W├дchter sch├╝tzen ihn die Pani’s, leer ist der Ort, umsonst bist du gekommen.┬л

Jamison Brereton

[Saram─Б:] The seers, sharpened by soma, will come here to this
place: Ay─Бsya [=Indra], the Aс╣Еgirases, and the Navagvas.
They will divide up this pen of cattle. Then will the Paс╣Зis just vomit this speech (of theirs)!

Griffith

Rsis will come inspirited with Soma, Angirases unwearied, and Navagvas.
This stall of cattle will they part among them: then will the Panis wish these words unspoken.

Macdonell

Hither will come the seers inspired with Soma, Ay─Бsya, Aс╣Еgirases, and Navagvas: They will appropriate this stall of cattle. The Paс╣Зis then shall all these boasts relinquish.

Geldner

Es werden die Rishi┬┤s, durch Soma scharf gemacht, hierher kommen: Ayasya, die Angiras┬┤ und Navagva┬┤s. Die werden die eingesperrte Herde der K├╝he unter sich teilen. Dann sollen die Pani┬┤s dieses Wort sich entfahren lassen!

Grassmann

┬╗Her werden kommen trankerregt die S├дnger Aj─Бsia, die Angira’s, die Neuner; Die werden sich der K├╝he Stall vertheilen; dann wird die Pani’s dieses Worts gereuen.┬л

Jamison Brereton

[Paс╣Зi:] Even though you have come in this way, Saram─Б, compelled by divine power,
I shall make you my sister. Do not go back. We will give away a portion of the cows to you, fortunate one.1574 X.109

Griffith

Even thus, O Sarama, hast thou come hither, forced by celestial might to make the journey.
Turn thee not back, for thou shalt be our sister: O Blest One, we will give thee of the cattle.

Macdonell

And since, O Saram─Б, thus by compulsion Divine coerced, thou hast come hither to us: We will make thee our sister: pray return not; We will give thee a share of kine, thou fair one.

Geldner

Da du, Sarama, nun einmal gekommen bist, durch g├╢ttliche Gewalt gen├╢tigt, so will ich dich zur Schwester machen. Geh nicht zur├╝ck; wir wollen dir, o Holde, von den K├╝hen welche abgeben.

Grassmann

┬╗Du bist gewiss, o Saram─Б, gekommen, gezwungen nur durch die Gewalt der G├╢tter; So geh nicht fort und werde unsre Schwester, wir geben, sch├╢ne, dir von unsern K├╝hen.┬л

Jamison Brereton

[Saram─Б:] I know no brotherhood and no sisterhood. Indra and the terrifying Aс╣Еgirases, they know (these things).
They seemed to me desirous of cattle when I came. Go away from here, Paс╣Зis, a very long way!

Griffith

Brotherhood, sisterhood, I know not either: the dread Angirases and Indra know them.
They seemed to long for kine when I departed. Hence, into distance, be ye gone, O Panis.

Macdonell

I know not what’s a brother or a sister: The fierce Aс╣Еgirases and Indra know it. They seemed to me, when I came here, right eager For kine: from hence go far away, ye Paс╣Зis.

Geldner

Von Bruder- und Schwesternschaft will ich nichts wissen; das wissen Indra und die furchtgebietenden Angiras┬┤. Sie schienen mir voll verlangen nach K├╝hen, als ich ging. Hebt euch weit weg von dannen, ihr Pani┬┤s!

Grassmann

┬╗Nicht Br├╝derschaft, nicht Schwesterschaft begehr’ ich; die grausen Angira’s und Indra wissen’s, Sie schienen, da ich ging, nach K├╝hen l├╝stern, geht fort von hier, o Pani’s, in die Ferne.┬л
